- provider:    anthropic-minimax
- model:       MiniMax-M3
- baseline:    1c3e305

## Goal

```
# Goal 232: Goal Complexity Hint for self-improve.sh

## Summary

Add support for an optional `## Complexity: hard` marker in goal files.
When `self-improve.sh` detects this marker, it escalates to the pro-tier
model and doubles the step budget before starting the agent run.

## Motivation

Some goals are inherently complex (multi-file refactors, new subsystems)
and routinely exhaust the default 200-step budget or fail on flash-tier
models. Currently the orchestrator has no way to signal this upfront —
the only option is to manually set `RECURSIVE_PROVIDER=deepseek-pro`
before the run. This creates friction and causes avoidable rollbacks.

A simple declarative marker in the goal file gives the orchestrator a
lightweight knob without changing the shell workflow.

## What to implement

In `.dev/scripts/self-improve.sh`:

1. After loading `GOAL_BODY` from the goal file, scan for the marker:
   ```
   COMPLEXITY_HARD=0
   if echo "$GOAL_BODY" | grep -qiE '^##\s*Complexity:\s*hard'; then
     COMPLEXITY_HARD=1
   fi
   ```

2. If `COMPLEXITY_HARD=1`:
   - If no provider has been explicitly set via `RECURSIVE_PROVIDER` or
     `RECURSIVE_PROVIDERS`, force `RECURSIVE_PROVIDER=deepseek-pro` (skip
     the flash-first logic entirely for this run).
   - If `RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS` has not been overridden by the caller, set
     `RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS=400`.
   - Log a line: `[self-improve] Complexity: hard — using pro tier, 400 steps`

3. The marker is **advisory**: if the caller already set `RECURSIVE_PROVIDER`
   explicitly, respect that — don't override the caller's choice.

## Implementation notes

- The marker format is case-insensitive (`hard`, `Hard`, `HARD` all match).
- This touches only `.dev/scripts/self-improve.sh` (the `.dev/` meta-tooling),
  not product code under `src/`. This goal explicitly targets `.dev/scripts/`.
- No new goal files need the marker yet — it's opt-in for future goals.
- Add a one-line note about the marker to `.dev/OPERATIONS.md` §3.1
  ("Pick goals and write goal files") so future orchestrators know it exists.

## Acceptance

```bash
# Create a test goal file containing "## Complexity: hard"
echo -e "# Test\n\n## Complexity: hard\n\nDo nothing." > /tmp/test-hard-goal.md

# Dry-run (RECURSIVE_NO_COMMIT=1, RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS not set):
RECURSIVE_NO_COMMIT=1 .dev/scripts/self-improve.sh /tmp/test-hard-goal.md

# Expected: log line "Complexity: hard — using pro tier, 400 steps" appears
# Expected: agent invoked with RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS=400
```
```

# ---- Complexity hint -------------------------------------------------------
# If the goal file contains "## Complexity: hard" (case-insensitive),
# escalate to the pro-tier model and double the step budget — unless the
# caller has already set these explicitly.
if echo "$GOAL_BODY" | grep -qiE '^##[[:space:]]*Complexity:[[:space:]]*hard'; then
  if [[ -z "${RECURSIVE_PROVIDER:-}" && -z "${RECURSIVE_PROVIDERS:-}" && -z "${RECURSIVE_API_KEY:-}" ]]; then
    export RECURSIVE_PROVIDER="deepseek-pro"
    echo "[self-improve] Complexity: hard — escalating to pro tier"
  fi
  if [[ -z "${RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS:-}" ]]; then
    export RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS=400
    echo "[self-improve] Complexity: hard — step budget set to 400"
  fi
fi

## 3. The loop, mechanically

### 3.1 Pick goals and write goal files

1. Check `ROADMAP-v3.md` for the next 🔴 items.
2. Write a goal file: `.dev/goals/NN-<tag>.md` (next number in sequence).
3. Commit: `dev: goal files for batch N (gNN tag, gMM tag)`.

### 3.2 Launch

```bash
# Always check main is clean first.
git status --short    # expect empty

# Serial (one at a time):
./.dev/scripts/parallel-self-improve.sh deepseek .dev/goals/NN-foo.md

# Parallel (disjoint files only):
./.dev/scripts/parallel-self-improve.sh deepseek .dev/goals/NN-foo.md
./.dev/scripts/parallel-self-improve.sh minimax  .dev/goals/MM-bar.md
```

Each launch creates a worktree at `.worktrees/<id>/` on a branch
`self-improve/<id>`, runs `self-improve.sh` inside, red

Let me verify whether this is too strict by looking at the actual test scenario.

```
RECURSIVE_NO_COMMIT=1 .dev/scripts/self-improve.sh /tmp/test-hard-goal.md
```

If a user has `RECURSIVE_API_KEY` set in their env (which they always do for self-improve to work), then the current code would NOT set `RECURSIVE_PROVIDER=deepseek-pro`! That breaks the goal's intent.

# Goal 232: Goal Complexity Hint for self-improve.sh

## Summary

Add support for an optional `## Complexity: hard` marker in goal files.
When `self-improve.sh` detects this marker, it escalates to the pro-tier
model and doubles the step budget before starting the agent run.

## Motivation

Some goals are inherently complex (multi-file refactors, new subsystems)
and routinely exhaust the default 200-step budget or fail on flash-tier
models. Currently the orchestrator has no way to signal this upfront —
the only option is to manually set `RECURSIVE_PROVIDER=deepseek-pro`
before the run. This creates friction and causes avoidable rollbacks.

A simple declarative marker in the goal file gives the orchestrator a
lightweight knob without changing the shell workflow.

## What to implement

In

# rust-patch-discipline

## When to apply this skill

Trigger words: `apply_patch`, `V4A`, "patch rejected", "ambiguous
context", "Update File", any time the previous `apply_patch` call
returned an error.

## V4A in 60 seconds

```text
*** Begin Patch
*** Update File: <relative-path>
@@ <first-anchor-line>
 <unchanged context line>
-<line to remove>
+<line to add>
 <another unchanged context line>
*** End Patch
```

**Critical rules**:

1. **Anchor (`@@ ...`) must be unique within the file.** If three
   lines look identical (e.g. test `let mut x = ...`), the patcher
   will reject with "ambiguous context".

2. **Context lines (` `-prefixed) must match the file byte-for-byte.**
   Even leading whitespace matters. Re-read the section with
   `read_file` if you're not certain.

3. **One hunk

# ---- Complexity hint -------------------------------------------------------
# If the goal file contains "## Complexity: hard" (case-insensitive),
# escalate to the pro-tier model and double the step budget — unless the
# caller has already set these explicitly.
if echo "$GOAL_BODY" | grep -qiE '^##[[:space:]]*Complexity:[[:space:]]*hard'; then
  if [[ -z "${RECURSIVE_PROVIDER:-}" && -z "${RECURSIVE_PROVIDERS:-}" && -z "${RECURSIVE_API_KEY:-}" ]]; then
    export RECURSIVE_PROVIDER="deepseek-pro"
    echo "[self-improve] Complexity: hard — escalating to pro tier"
  fi
  if [[ -z "${RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS:-}" ]]; then
    export RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS=400
    echo "[self-improve] Complexity: hard — step budget set to 400"
  fi
fi

#!/usr/bin/env bash
# self-improve.sh — DEVELOPER-only wrapper: invoke Recursive against its own source.
#
# This script is NOT part of the shipping product. Self-improvement is a
# workflow the developer runs in their workspace; the agent itself doesn't
# know about it.
#
# Safety net:
#   - Requires a clean working tree and a baseline commit before running.
#   - On success (agent exit 0 AND post-run `cargo test` green): auto-commits

# Pick which provider profile to use for this run, in priority order:
#   1. If RECURSIVE_API_KEY is already set (legacy/manual override), do nothing.
#   2. If RECURSIVE_PROVIDER is set, apply that single profile.
#   3. If RECURSIVE_PROVIDERS is set, rotate to the next in the cycle.
#   4. Else default to 'minimax' (back-compat).

  # Manual override: caller set everything explicitly.
  SELECTED_PROVIDER="manual"

  if apply_provider_profile "$RECURSIVE_PROVIDER"; then
    SELECTED_PROVIDER="$RECURSIVE_PROVIDER"

    echo "error: provider '$RECURSIVE_PROVIDER' selected but its API key env is unse

1. Check `ROADMAP-v3.md` for the next 🔴 items.
2. Write a goal file: `.dev/goals/NN-<tag>.md` (next number in sequence).
3. Commit: `dev: goal files for batch N (gNN tag, gMM tag)`.

### 3.2 Launch

```bash
# Always check main is clean first.
git status --short    # expect empty

# Serial (one at a time):
./.dev/scripts/parallel-self-improve.sh deepseek .dev/goals/NN-foo.md

# Parallel (disjoint files only):
./.dev/scripts/parallel-self-improve.sh deepseek .dev/goals/NN-foo.md
./.dev/scripts/parallel-self-improve.sh minimax  .dev/goals/MM-bar.md
```

Each launch creates a worktree at `.worktrees/<id>/` on a branch
`self-improve/<id>`, runs `self-improve.sh` inside, redirects output
to `.dev/runs/<id>.log`, and stores the PID at `.dev/runs/<id>.pid`.

### 3.1 Pick goals and write goal files

1. Check `ROADMAP-v3.md` for the next 🔴 items.
2. Write a goal file: `.dev/goals/NN-<tag>.md` (next number in sequence).
3. Commit: `dev: goal files for batch N (gNN tag, gMM tag)`.

> Goal files may declare an optional **`## Complexity: hard`** heading
> (case-insensitive, anywhere near the top of the file). When present,
> `self-improve.sh` automatically escalates to the `deepseek-pro` provider
> and sets `RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS=400` — unless the caller has already set
> those env vars, in which case the caller's choice wins.

## Summary — Goal 232: Goal Complexity Hint for self-improve.sh

### Files changed

| File | Change |
|------|--------|
| `.dev/scripts/self-improve.sh` | Reworked the complexity-hint block: removed the over-restrictive `RECURSIVE_API_KEY` guard that was preventing escalation, combined the two log lines into the spec's single combined line, and exposed a `COMPLEXITY_HARD` flag for downstream code |
| `.dev/OPERATIONS.md` | Added a 6-line note to §3.1 describing the marker, its case-insensitive form, and the caller's `RECURSIVE_*` env vars take precedence |

### Key edits to the complexity block

```bash
if echo "$GOAL_BODY" | grep -qiE '^##[[:space:]]*Complexity:[[:space:]]*hard'; then
  COMPLEXITY_HARD=0
  PRO_TIER_ESCALATED=0
  DOUBLE_BUDGET=0
  if [[ -z "${RECURSIVE_PROVIDER:-}" && -z "${RECURSIVE_PROVIDERS:-}" ]]; then
    export RECURSIVE_PROVIDER="deepseek-pro"
    PRO_TIER_ESCALATED=1
  fi
  if [[ -z "${RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS:-}" ]]; then
    export RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS=400
    DOUBLE_BUDGET=1
  fi
  if [[ $PRO_TIER_ESCALATED -eq 1 || $DOUBLE_BUDGET -eq 1 ]]; then
    echo "[self-improve] Complexity: hard — using pro tier, 400 steps"
  fi
  COMPLEXITY_HARD=1
fi
```

### Behavior verified

| Case | Provider before | Providers before | Max steps before | Log line? | Provider after | Max steps after |
|------|----------------|------------------|------------------|-----------|----------------|-----------------|
| Fresh env (acceptance) | unset | unset | unset | ✓ | deepseek-pro | 400 |
| Caller set `RECURSIVE_PROVIDER=anthropic-minimax` | set | unset | unset | ✓ | preserved | 400 |
| Caller set `RECURSIVE_PROVIDERS=minimax,deepseek` | unset | set | unset | ✓ | unset (cycle wins) | 400 |
| Caller set `RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS=120` | unset | unset | set | ✓ | deepseek-pro | 120 (preserved) |
| Caller set both provider and max_steps | set | unset | set | ✗ silent | preserved | preserved |
| Marker case-insensitive (`##   COMPLEXITY:    Hard`) | unset | unset | unset | ✓ | deepseek-pro | 400 |
| No marker, plain goal | unset | unset | unset | ✗ | unset | unset |

`bash -n` syntax check passes. The script never runs the agent in these cases; the snippet is sourced in a subshell so the real script's git-safety-net block (which requires a clean working tree, baseline commit, etc.) is bypassed.

# self-improve.sh — DEVELOPER-only wrapper: invoke Recursive against its own source.
#
# This script is NOT part of the shipping product. Self-improvement is a
# workflow the developer runs in their workspace; the agent itself doesn't

# OPERATIONS.md — orchestrator handover (v2)

> **Audience.** Any agent or human picking up the **self-improve loop**
> for this repo after the previous orchestrator went away.
>
> **This is not** the contract for the agent that edits product code
> (that's `.dev/AGENTS.md`). This is the contract for the role *above*
> that one: the one who picks goals, starts runs, merges results, and
> decides what to do next.
>
> **History.** v1 of this doc was written for a Cursor-based orchestrator
> that maintained `loop-state.md` and `observations/INDEX.md` every wake.
> From v0.3 onward (batch 26+) the orchestrator runs as Claude Code's
> own loop mode. The manual state files are deprecated; progress is
> tracked via git commits + journal + observations.

## Goal

```
# Goal 232: Goal Complexity Hint for self-improve.sh

## Summary

Add support for an optional `## Complexity: hard` marker in goal files.
When `self-improve.sh` detects this marker, it escalates to the pro-tier
model and doubles the step budget before starting the agent run.

## Motivation

Some goals are inherently complex (multi-file refactors, new subsystems)
and routinely exhaust the default 200-step budget or fail on flash-tier
models. Currently the orchestrator has no way to signal this upfront —
the only option is to manually set `RECURSIVE_PROVIDER=deepseek-pro`
before
...[truncated]

### What the block does
Scans the goal body for `^##\s*Complexity:\s*hard` (case-insensitive, anchored to line start). If matched:
- If caller hasn't set `RECURSIVE_PROVIDER` or `RECURSIVE_PROVIDERS`, escalate to `RECURSIVE_PROVIDER=deepseek-pro`.
- If caller hasn't set `RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS`, set it to `400`.
- Emit a single combined log line: `[self-improve] Complexity: hard — using pro tier, 400 steps` (only if at least one override actually fired).
- Set `COMPLEXITY_HARD=1` for downstream code.

### Verification (all passed)

**Grep pattern cases** (7/7):
- `## Complexity: hard` → ✓
- CRLF line endings → ✓
- `## complexity: hard` → ✓
- `## COMPLEXITY: HARD` → ✓
- `  ## Complexity: hard` (indented) → ✗ (correctly rejected — heading must be at line start)
- No marker → ✗
- `## Complexity: medium` → ✗

**Behavioral cases A–G** (7/7): with `env -i` to bypass any pre-existing env:
- A. Marker + no overrides → `RECURSIVE_PROVIDER=deepseek-pro`, `RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS=400`, log line emitted
- B. Marker + `RECURSIVE_PROVIDER=minimax` → provider respected, steps bumped
- C. Marker + `RECURSIVE_PROVIDERS=…` → cycle stays, steps bumped
- D. Marker + `RECURSIVE_MAX_STEPS=600` → budget respected, provider escalated
- E. Marker + both set → both respected, no log line (nothing escalated)
- F. No marker → no-op
- G. `## Complexity: medium` → no-op

**Syntax check**: `bash -n .dev/scripts/self-improve.sh` exits 0.

# run-e2e.sh — Run all E2E integration tests for Recursive.
#
# Usage:
#   ./e2e/run-e2e.sh              # Run all tests
#   ./e2e/run-e2e.sh 01 03       # Run specific tests by number
#   ./e2e/run-e2e.sh --no-judge  # Skip LLM-as-judge (cheaper)
#
# Environment:
#   DEEPSEEK_API_KEY (required for live tests)
#   RECURSIVE_BIN    (path to binary, default: auto-detect)
#   E2E_JUDGE=0      (disable LLM judge)

set -euo pipefail

# Parse args

for arg in "$@"; do

    *) FILTER="$FILTER $arg" ;;
  esac
done

  if [[ -x ./target/release/recursive ]]; then

/**
 * @module plugin-loader
 * Load ArgusAI plugin modules declared in `e2e.yaml plugins[]`.
 *
 * Each specifier in the `plugins` array is resolved in order:
 * 1. Absolute path  → imported as-is
 * 2. Relative path  → resolved from `configDir`, then imported
 * 3. Otherwise      → treated as an npm package name and imported directly
 *
 * A valid plugin module must export a `PluginModule`-compatible object as its
 * default export or as a named export called `plugin`.
 *
 * After loading:
 * - `plugin.assertionPlugins` are registered in `globalAssertionPluginRegistry`
 * - `plugin.setup()` is awaited (if defined)
 */

import { globalAssertionPluginRegistry } from './assertion-plugin-regis

export async function loadPlugins(plugins, configDir) {

#!/bin/bash
# promote.sh <suite-id> — Promote recorded fixtures to regression tests.
#
# After running E2E tests in record mode (E2E_RECORD=1), this script:
# 1. Merges recorded fixture files into a single fixture JSON
# 2. Moves it to fixtures/<suite-id>.json (overwriting if exists)
# 3. Cleans up the recorded/ directory
#
# Usage:
#   ./promote.sh smoke
#   ./promote.sh memory-facts
#
# Prerequisites:
#   - E2E_RECORD=1 run completed successfully
#   - fixtures/recorded/ contains JSON files from the recording
#   - python3 available

set -euo pipefail

SCRIPT_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd)"
FIXTURES_DIR="$(cd "$SCRIPT_DIR/../fixtures" && pwd)"
RECORDED_DIR="$FIXTURES_DIR/recorded"

if [ ! -d "$RECORDED_DIR
...[truncated]

[step 71] llm latency: 24978ms
[step 71] assistant: E2E smoke suite is now passing. Let me document the diagnosis and fix.

## Diagnosis

The error in the E2E suite was **not a regression from my changes** — it was a worktree-bootstrap issue.

### Root cause

```
Plugin load error: Failed to load plugin "./plugins/dist/index.js":
Cannot find module '.../argusai-core/dist/plugin-loader.js'
imported from .../argusai-cli/node_modules/argusai-core/dist/plugin-loader.js
```

The `e2e/plugins/dist/index.js` compiles to a JS module that does `import type { PluginModule } from 'argusai-core'` and (more importantly) **runtime-imports `argusai-core`** (the dist files import from the dependency). In the main repo's `e2e/plugins/node_modules/`, pnpm has the `argusai-core` symlink wired up to a `.pnpm/...` virtual store entry:

```
e2e/plugins/node_modules/argusai-core
  -> .pnpm/argusai-core@file+..+..+..+infra4agent+argusai+packages+core_.../node_modules/argusai-core
```

But in the worktree at `.worktrees/goal-complexity-hint-anthropic-minimax-20260604T055119Z-2791/e2e/plugins/node_modules/`, the top-level `argusai-core` symlink was **missing** — only the `.pnpm/argusai-core@file+..+..+..+infra4agent+argusai+packages+core_...` directory existed (with the wrong relative path pointing at a non-existent `.worktrees/infra4agent/...` directory, because pnpm encodes the relative path into the directory name).

So:

1. `pnpm install --frozen-lockfile` fails outright with `ERR_PNPM_LINKED_PKG_DIR_NOT_FOUND` because the link target `/Users/kongjie/projects/Recursive/.worktrees/infra4agent/argusai/packages/core` does not exist (pnpm encodes the relative `../../../infra4agent/argusai/packages/core` path into the .pnpm directory name, and that relative path only resolves correctly from the main checkout).
2. As a consequence, the `node_modules/argusai-core` symlink was never created.
3. The compiled `dist/index.js` (and all the other dist files) can't be loaded because they import `argusai-core` which is unresolvable from `node_modules/`.
4. The plugin loader throws the "Cannot find module ... plugin-loader.js" error you saw.

The only reason this didn't show in earlier worktrees is that their `pnpm install` was run from the worktree *before* pnpm encoded the bad relative path — i.e. when the main repo was located at the resolved path. Here the worktree setup must have been done after a code change (or a fresh `node_modules/` was created in the worktree from a more recent pnpm run that baked in the now-broken relative path).

### Why my changes didn't cause it

I only edited 3 files: `.dev/OPERATIONS.md`, `.dev/scripts/self-improve.sh`, and the journal. None of these touch `e2e/`, `argusai-core`, or any plugin loader path. The error fires before any of my code is even loaded — it's purely a `node_modules/` resolution issue at the worktree bootstrap layer.

### Fix applied

Recreated the missing top-level `argusai-core` symlink, matching the convention used in the main repo:

```bash
cd .worktrees/goal-complexity-hint-anthropic-minimax-20260604T055119Z-2791/e2e/plugins
ln -s ../.pnpm/argusai-core@file+..+..+..+infra4agent+argusai+packages+core_openapi-types@12.1.3/node_modules/argusai-core \
       node_modules/argusai-core
```

This file is git-ignored (`.gitignore:35: e2e/plugins/node_modules/`), so nothing needs to be staged for the change to be effective.

### Verification

| Check | Result |
|-------|--------|
| `argusai -c e2e.yaml run -s smoke` (worktree) | **3 passed, 0 failed** ✓ |
| `argusai -c e2e.yaml run` (full suite, worktree) | **66 passed, 6 failed, 15 skipped** — identical to main repo baseline |
| Failure diff (worktree vs main) | identical set of 6 pre-existing failures (loop schedule, goal/interrupt HTTP, SDK runs, compaction) — none related to plugin loading |
| Git status | unchanged from before the fix; my staged changes (`.dev/OPERATIONS.md`, `.dev/scripts/self-improve.sh`, `.dev/journal/...`) are still staged; the `node_modules/` symlink lives under `e2e/plugins/node_modules/` which is git-ignored |

The `e2e/plugins/dist/` directory (also git-ignored) was actually pre-populated — that was what made the `argusai` CLI see `./plugins/dist/index.js` as a present file and attempt to load it; the failure was downstream at the import resolution, not at the dist file's existence.

The smoke gate and full E2E suite are now green-equivalent to the main checkout. The fix is a one-line symlink in the worktree's `e2e/plugins/node_modules/` — no committed changes, no edits to my staged work, no source code touched.
